GT Equivalence Verification (MatSci12)
============================================================
GT: c0*epsilon*(-c1*(T - c2) + c3) + c4*epsilon**c5*exp(-c6/(c7*T)) + epsilon*c8*exp(-(T - c9)**c10)
Candidates evaluated: 50
Matched candidate IDs: []
Matched candidates: []

I need to analyze whether any candidate can be made mathematically equivalent to the Ground Truth (GT).

**GT expression:**
```
3.6246*epsilon*(-0.05899*(T - 367.02) + 1) + 94.205*epsilon^0.4475*exp(-55.016/(8.314*T)) + epsilon*5.1243*exp(-(T - 367.02)^2)
```

Let me expand the GT:
- Term 1: `3.6246*epsilon*(-0.05899*T + 0.05899*367.02 + 1)` = `3.6246*epsilon*(-0.05899*T + 22.65)` ≈ `-0.2139*epsilon*T + 82.08*epsilon`
- Term 2: `94.205*epsilon^0.4475*exp(-6.616/T)`
- Term 3: `5.1243*epsilon*exp(-(T-367.02)^2)`

The GT has these key structural features:
1. A term linear in `epsilon*T`
2. A term linear in `epsilon`
3. A term with `epsilon^0.4475` (fractional power) multiplied by `exp(-const/T)` (Arrhenius-type)
4. A term with `epsilon*exp(-(T-367)^2)` (Gaussian in T)

The critical observation is that the GT contains:
- `exp(-c/T)`: an Arrhenius/exponential term in 1/T
- `exp(-(T-c)^2)`: a Gaussian term in T

None of the candidates contain `exp()` functions at all. Let me verify this by scanning all candidates:

Looking through all 50 candidates, I see terms like:
- Polynomials in epsilon and T
- `epsilon**c` (power law)
- `Max(0, c + epsilon)**(1/3)` or `**2`
- `cos(T)` (in candidates 29-33)
- Rational functions (candidate 1)

**No candidate contains `exp()` terms.**

The GT has `exp(-55.016/(8.314*T))` and `exp(-(T-367)^2)`. These are fundamentally non-polynomial, non-trigonometric functions of T. They cannot be represented by:
- Polynomials in T
- `cos(T)` 
- Rational functions in T
- Power laws in epsilon alone

The exponential terms are essential parts of the GT (with significant coefficients: 94.205 and 5.1243), and they depend on T in ways that cannot be replicated by any of the basis functions present in the candidates.

By the principle of linear independence of basis functions (Rule 3), exponential functions like `exp(-c/T)` and `exp(-(T-c)^2)` cannot be expressed as polynomials, trigonometric functions, or power laws. These are fundamentally different function classes.

Therefore, **none of the candidates can match the GT**.
